			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<p><b>Caterpillar Inc.</b> (sometimes shortened to <b>CAT</b>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Fortune_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortune 100">Fortune 100</a> corporation which designs, develops, engineers, manufactures, markets and sells <a href="/wiki/Heavy_equipment_(construction)" class="mw-redirect" title="Heavy equipment (construction)">machinery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">engines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial products</a> and insurance to customers via a worldwide <a href="/wiki/Dealer_(franchising)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dealer (franchising)">dealer</a> network. It is the world's largest construction equipment manufacturer.<sup id="cite_ref-about_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10K_2009_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K_2009-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>
In 2018, Caterpillar was ranked #65 on the Fortune 500 list<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> and #238 on the Global Fortune 500 list.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Caterpillar <a href="/wiki/Stock" title="Stock">stock</a> is a component of the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-2018SEC_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018SEC-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">101,500 (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-2017SEC_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2017SEC-2">[2]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none; padding:0;">
<div class="NavHead" style="font-size: 105%; background: transparent; text-align: left;"><small>Subsidiary List</small></div>
<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">Caterpillar Financial Services</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">Caterpillar Insurance Holdings</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">Caterpillar Logistics Services</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">Caterpillar Marine Power Systems</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0">FG Wilson</li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Perkins_Engines" title="Perkins Engines">Perkins Engines</a></li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Progress_Rail_Services" title="Progress Rail Services">Progress Rail Services</a></li><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><a href="/wiki/Solar_Turbines" title="Solar Turbines">Solar Turbines</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://caterpillar.com">caterpillar<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-about_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10K_2009_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K_2009-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haddock-37_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haddock-37-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4Q2010_Earnings_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Q2010_Earnings-6">[6]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Caterpillar Inc. traces its origins to the 1925 merger of the <a href="/wiki/Holt_Manufacturing_Company" title="Holt Manufacturing Company">Holt Manufacturing Company</a> and the <a href="/wiki/C._L._Best" title="C. L. Best">C. L. Best Tractor Company</a>, creating a new entity, the California-based Caterpillar Tractor Company.<sup id="cite_ref-lehman_deals_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lehman_deals-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1986, the company reorganized itself as a Delaware corporation under the current name, Caterpillar Inc. Caterpillar's headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Deerfield,_Illinois" title="Deerfield, Illinois">Deerfield, Illinois</a>; it announced in January 2017 that over the course of that year it would relocate its headquarters from Peoria, Illinois, to Deerfield, Illinois, scrapping plans from 2015 of building an $800 million new headquarters complex in downtown Peoria.<sup id="cite_ref-PStar2017_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PStar2017-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p><p>The company also licenses and markets a line of clothing and workwear boots under its Cat / Caterpillar name.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> 
Caterpillar machinery is recognizable by its trademark "Caterpillar Yellow" <a href="/wiki/Livery" title="Livery">livery</a> and the "CAT" logo.<sup id="cite_ref-tmyellow_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tmyellow-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15-08-historischesRaupenfahrzeug_IMG_1446.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/15-08-historischesRaupenfahrzeug_IMG_1446.JPG/220px-15-08-historischesRaupenfahrzeug_IMG_1446.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/15-08-historischesRaupenfahrzeug_IMG_1446.JPG/220px-15-08-historischesRaupenfahrzeug_IMG_1446.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15-08-historischesRaupenfahrzeug_IMG_1446.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HOLT (before 1925)</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Holt_Manufacturing_Company" title="Holt Manufacturing Company">Holt Manufacturing Company</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BenjaminHolt.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/BenjaminHolt.jpg/220px-BenjaminHolt.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="276" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="376"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 276px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/BenjaminHolt.jpg/220px-BenjaminHolt.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="276" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BenjaminHolt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Holt" title="Benjamin Holt">Benjamin Holt</a>, one of the founding fathers of <a href="/wiki/Holt_Manufacturing_Company" title="Holt Manufacturing Company">Holt Manufacturing Company</a>.</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The steam tractors of the 1890s and early 1900s were extremely heavy, sometimes weighing 1,000 pounds (450 kg) per <a href="/wiki/Horsepower" title="Horsepower">horsepower</a>, and often sank into the rich, soft earth of the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_%E2%80%93_San_Joaquin_River_Delta" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacramento – San Joaquin River Delta">San Joaquin Valley Delta</a> farmland surrounding <a href="/wiki/Stockton,_California" title="Stockton, California">Stockton, California</a>. <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Holt" title="Benjamin Holt">Benjamin Holt</a> attempted to fix the problem by increasing the size and width of the wheels up to 7.5 feet (2.3 m) tall and 6 feet (1.8 m) wide, producing a tractor 46 feet (14 m) wide. But this also made the tractors increasingly complex, expensive and difficult to maintain.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cat45-mojave.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Cat45-mojave.jpg/220px-Cat45-mojave.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="466"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 160px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Cat45-mojave.jpg/220px-Cat45-mojave.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="160" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cat45-mojave.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two <a href="/wiki/Holt_tractor" title="Holt tractor">Holt 45</a> gas crawler tractors team up to pull a long wagon train in the <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">Mojave Desert</a> during construction of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Aqueduct" title="Los Angeles Aqueduct">Los Angeles Aqueduct</a> in 1909.</div></div></div>
<p>Another solution considered was to lay a temporary <a href="/wiki/Plank_road" title="Plank road">plank road</a> ahead of the steam tractor, but this was time-consuming, expensive, and interfered with earthmoving. Holt thought of wrapping the planks around the wheels. He replaced the wheels on a 40 horsepower (30 kW) Holt steamer, No. 77, with a set of wooden tracks bolted to chains. On Thanksgiving Day, November 24, 1904, he successfully tested the updated machine plowing the soggy <a href="/wiki/Delta_(landform)" class="mw-redirect" title="Delta (landform)">delta land</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_%E2%80%93_San_Joaquin_River_Delta" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacramento – San Joaquin River Delta">Roberts Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-laird_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laird-16">[16]</a></sup></p><p>Contemporaneously <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hornsby_%26_Sons" title="Richard Hornsby &amp; Sons">Richard Hornsby &amp; Sons</a> in Grantham, Lincolnshire, England, developed a steel plate tracked vehicle which it patented in 1904. This tractor steered by differential braking of the tracks and did not require the forward tiller steering wheel for steering making it the first to do so.  Several tractors were made and sold to operate in the Yukon, one example of which was in operation until 1927 remnants of which still exist to this day. However, Hornsby were unable to interest the British Military in 1907, although soldiers who witnessed the trials nicknamed the machine a caterpillar.  Hornsby therefore found a limited market for their tractor so they sold their patent to Holt in 1911, the same year Holt trademarked "Caterpillar".
</p><p>Company photographer Charles Clements was reported to have observed that the tractor crawled like a <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar" title="Caterpillar">caterpillar</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-about-inventors_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-inventors-17">[17]</a></sup> and Holt seized on the metaphor. "Caterpillar it is. That's the name for it!"<sup id="cite_ref-laird_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laird-16">[16]</a></sup> Some sources, though, attribute this name to British soldiers in July 1907. Two years later Holt sold his first steam-powered tractor crawlers for US$5,500, about US$128,000 today. Each side featured a track frame measured 30 inches (760 mm) high by 42 inches (1,100 mm) wide and were 9 feet (2.7 m) long. The tracks were 3 inches (76 mm) by 4 inches (100 mm) <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_sempervirens" title="Sequoia sempervirens">redwood</a> slats.<sup id="cite_ref-laird_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laird-16">[16]</a></sup></p><p>Holt received the first <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patent</a> for a practical <a href="/wiki/Continuous_track" title="Continuous track">continuous track</a> for use with a tractor on December 7, 1907, for his improved "Traction Engine" ("improvement in vehicles, and especially of the traction engine class; and included endless traveling platform supports upon which the engine is carried").<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Initial_Establishment_in_Peoria_.281910.29_and_Headquarters_Move_to_Deerfield_.282017.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_Establishment_in_Peoria_(1910)_and_Headquarters_Move_to_Deerfield_(2017)">Initial Establishment in Peoria (1910) and Headquarters Move to Deerfield (2017)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Initial Establishment in Peoria (1910) and Headquarters Move to Deerfield (2017)" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Caterpillar_Tractor_Co._Factory,_Peoria,_Ill.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_Caterpillar_Tractor_Co._Factory%2C_Peoria%2C_Ill.jpg/220px-The_Caterpillar_Tractor_Co._Factory%2C_Peoria%2C_Ill.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="947"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 139px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/The_Caterpillar_Tractor_Co._Factory%2C_Peoria%2C_Ill.jpg/220px-The_Caterpillar_Tractor_Co._Factory%2C_Peoria%2C_Ill.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="139" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Caterpillar_Tractor_Co._Factory,_Peoria,_Ill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A postcard showing the Caterpillar Tractor Co. plant in <a href="/wiki/East_Peoria" class="mw-redirect" title="East Peoria">Peoria</a>, period 1930–1945.</div></div></div>
<p>On February 2, 1910,<sup id="cite_ref-acmoc2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acmoc2-19">[19]</a></sup> Holt opened up a plant in <a href="/wiki/East_Peoria" class="mw-redirect" title="East Peoria">East Peoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, led by his nephew Pliny Holt. There Pliny met farm implement dealer <a href="/wiki/Murray_M._Baker" title="Murray M. Baker">Murray Baker</a> who knew of an empty factory that had been recently built to manufacture farm implements and steam <a href="/wiki/Traction_engine" title="Traction engine">traction engines</a>. Baker, who later became the first executive vice president of what became Caterpillar Tractor Company, wrote to Holt headquarters in Stockton and described the plant of the bankrupt Colean Manufacturing Co. of <a href="/wiki/East_Peoria,_Illinois" title="East Peoria, Illinois">East Peoria, Illinois</a>.
On October 25, 1909, Pliny Holt purchased the factory,<sup id="cite_ref-leffingwell_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leffingwell-20">[20]</a></sup> and immediately began operations with 12 employees.<sup id="cite_ref-gordon_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordon-21">[21]</a></sup> Holt incorporated it as the Holt Caterpillar Company, although he did not trademark the name <i>Caterpillar</i> until August 2, 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-acmoc2_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acmoc2-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>The addition of a plant in the <a href="/wiki/Midwest" class="mw-redirect" title="Midwest">Midwest</a>, despite the hefty <a href="/wiki/Capital_(economics)" title="Capital (economics)">capital</a> needed to retool the plant, proved so profitable that only two years later the company employed 625 people and was exporting tractors to <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, Canada, and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-idch_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idch-22">[22]</a></sup> Tractors were built in both Stockton and East Peoria.<sup id="cite_ref-orleman_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orleman-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>On January 31, 2017, after more than 90 years of being headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Peoria,_Illinois" title="Peoria, Illinois">Peoria, Illinois</a>, the company announced plans to move their headquarters from Peoria to <a href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago, Illinois</a> by the end of 2017. The upper echelon of executives, including newly installed CEO Jim Umpleby, would begin relocating later that year, with up to 100 employees total moving by year's end. About 300 employees will work in the new office at an as-yet undecided location once the transition is complete. The company indefinitely suspended planning for the new Peoria headquarters in the fall of 2015 after announcing a restructuring effort that called for up to 10,000 jobs to be cut and about 20 facilities around the world to be closed or consolidated. The changes contributed to $2.3 billion in savings in 2016, but sales and revenue for last year still were more than 40 percent below peak levels of 2012. Umpleby said that decline is a fundamental reason the company's board of directors opted to move global headquarters to an area where the global marketplace is in easier reach.<sup id="cite_ref-PStar2017_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PStar2017-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>The site finally selected at 500 Lake Cook Road in <a href="/wiki/Deerfield,_Illinois" title="Deerfield, Illinois">Deerfield, Illinois</a> had for many years been the location of a <a href="/wiki/Fiatallis" title="Fiatallis">Fiatallis</a> facility producing wheel loaders.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_in_World_War_I">Use in World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Use in World War I" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The first tanks used in WW1 were manufactured by William Foster &amp; Co. also in Lincolnshire and were introduced to the battlefield in 1916.  That company had collaborated with Hornsby in the development of the vehicles demonstrated to the British military in 1907, providing the paraffin (kerosene) engines.
</p><p>Holt's track-type tractors played a support role in World War I. Even before the U.S. formally entered WWI, Holt had shipped 1,200 tractors to England, France and Russia for agricultural purposes. These governments, however, sent the tractors directly to the battlefront where the military put them to work hauling artillery and supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> broke out, the British War Office ordered a Holt tractor and put it through trials at <a href="/wiki/Aldershot" title="Aldershot">Aldershot</a>. The War Office was suitably impressed and chose it as a gun-tractor.<sup id="cite_ref-historic_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historic-26">[26]</a></sup> Over the next four years, the Holt tractor became a major <a href="/wiki/Artillery_tractor" title="Artillery tractor">artillery tractor</a>, mainly used to haul medium guns like the <a href="/wiki/6_inch_26_cwt_howitzer" class="mw-redirect" title="6 inch 26 cwt howitzer">6-inch howitzer</a>, the <a href="/wiki/BL_60_pounder_gun" class="mw-redirect" title="BL 60 pounder gun">60-pounder</a>, and later the <a href="/wiki/BL_9.2_inch_Howitzer" class="mw-redirect" title="BL 9.2 inch Howitzer">9.2-inch</a> howitzer.<sup id="cite_ref-freeserver_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freeserver-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>Holt tractors were also the inspiration for the development of the British <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tank</a>, which profoundly altered ground warfare tactics.<sup id="cite_ref-laird_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-laird-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Major <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Dunlop_Swinton" class="mw-redirect" title="Ernest Dunlop Swinton">Ernest Swinton</a>, sent to France as an army <a href="/wiki/War_correspondent" title="War correspondent">war correspondent</a>, very soon saw the potential of a track-laying tractor.<sup id="cite_ref-swinton_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swinton-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>116</span></sup> Although the British later chose an English firm to build its first tanks, the Holt tractor became "one of the most important military vehicles of all time."<sup id="cite_ref-freeserver_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freeserver-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Serpentine_vtm_cat_d2_gnangarra.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Serpentine_vtm_cat_d2_gnangarra.jpg/220px-Serpentine_vtm_cat_d2_gnangarra.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Serpentine_vtm_cat_d2_gnangarra.jpg/220px-Serpentine_vtm_cat_d2_gnangarra.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Serpentine_vtm_cat_d2_gnangarra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_D2" title="Caterpillar D2">Caterpillar D2</a>, introduced in 1938, at the Serpentine Vintage Tractor Museum, <a href="/wiki/Serpentine,_Western_Australia" title="Serpentine, Western Australia">Serpentine, Western Australia</a>.</div></div></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_challenges">Post-war challenges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-war challenges" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Holt tractors had become well known during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Military contracts formed the major part of the company's production. When the war ended, Holt's planned expansion to meet the military's needs was abruptly terminated. The heavy-duty tractors needed by the military were unsuitable for farmers. The company's situation worsened when artillery tractors were returned from Europe, depressing prices for new equipment and Holt's unsold inventory of military tractors. The company struggled with the transition from wartime boom to peacetime bust. To keep the company afloat, they borrowed heavily.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/C._L._Best" title="C. L. Best">C. L. Best Gas Tractor Company</a>, formed by Clarence Leo Best in 1910 and Holt's primary competitor, had during the war received government support enabling it to supply farmers with the smaller agricultural tractors they needed.<sup id="cite_ref-ohecat_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohecat-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-acmoc3_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acmoc3-31">[31]</a></sup> As a result, Best had gained a considerable market advantage over Holt by war's end. Best also assumed considerable debt to allow it to continue expansion, especially production of its new Best Model 60 "Tracklayer".
</p><p>Both companies were adversely impacted by the transition from a wartime to a peacetime economy, which contributed to a nationwide <a href="/wiki/Depression_of_1920%E2%80%9321" title="Depression of 1920–21">depression</a>, further inhibiting sales. On December 5, 1920, 71-year-old Benjamin Holt died after a month-long illness.<sup id="cite_ref-acmoc3_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acmoc3-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Caterpillar_company_formed_.281925.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Caterpillar_company_formed_(1925)">Caterpillar company formed (1925)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Caterpillar company formed (1925)" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caterpillar-60,_1931.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Caterpillar-60%2C_1931.jpg/220px-Caterpillar-60%2C_1931.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="296"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 130px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Caterpillar-60%2C_1931.jpg/220px-Caterpillar-60%2C_1931.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="130" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caterpillar-60,_1931.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 60-horsepower Caterpillar Sixty being used for road work in the <a href="/wiki/Cibola_National_Forest" title="Cibola National Forest">Cibola National Forest</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, United States in 1931</div></div></div>
<p>The banks and bankers who held the company's large debt forced the Holt board of directors to accept their candidate, Thomas A. Baxter, to succeed Benjamin Holt. Baxter initially cut the large tractors from the company's product line and introduced smaller models focused on the agricultural market. When the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aid_Highway_Act_of_1921_(Phipps_Act)" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Aid Highway Act of 1921 (Phipps Act)">Federal Aid Highway Act of 1921</a> funded a US$1 billion federal highway building program, Baxter began refocusing the company towards building road construction equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-leffingwell_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leffingwell-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>66</span></sup> Both companies also faced fierce competition from the <a href="/wiki/Fordson_tractor" class="mw-redirect" title="Fordson tractor">Fordson</a> company.
</p><p>Between 1907 and 1918, Best and Holt had spent about US$1.5 million in legal fees fighting each other in a number of <a href="/wiki/Breach_of_contract" title="Breach of contract">contractual</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trademark_infringement" title="Trademark infringement">trademark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patent_infringement" title="Patent infringement">patent infringement</a> lawsuits.<sup id="cite_ref-acmoc6_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-acmoc6-33">[33]</a></sup> Harry H. Fair of the bond brokerage house of Pierce, Fair &amp; Company of San Francisco had helped to finance C. L. Best's debt and Holt shareholders approached him about their company's financial difficulty. Fair recommended that the two companies should merge. In April and May 1925, the financially stronger C. L. Best merged with the market leader Holt Caterpillar to form the Caterpillar Tractor Co.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p><p>The new company was headquartered in San Leandro until 1930, when under the terms of the merger it was moved to Peoria.<sup id="cite_ref-gordon_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gordon-21">[21]</a></sup> Baxter had been removed as CEO earlier in 1925, and Clarence Leo Best assumed the title of CEO, and remained in that role until October 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-ohecat_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohecat-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>The Caterpillar company consolidated its product lines, offering only five track-type tractors: the <a href="/wiki/Holt_tractor#2_Ton" title="Holt tractor">2 Ton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holt_tractor#5_Ton" title="Holt tractor">5 Ton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Holt_tractor#10_Ton" title="Holt tractor">10 Ton</a> from the Holt Manufacturing Company's old product line and the <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_30" class="mw-redirect" title="Caterpillar 30">Caterpillar 30</a></span> and <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_60" class="mw-redirect" title="Caterpillar 60">Caterpillar 60</a></span> from the C. L. Best Tractor Co.'s former product line. The 10 Ton and 5 Ton models were discontinued in 1926. In 1928, the 2 Ton was discontinued. Sales the first year were US$13 million. By 1929, sales climbed to US$52.8 million, and Caterpillar continued to grow throughout the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> of the 1930s.
</p><p>Caterpillar adopted the <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engine</a> to replace gasoline engines. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Caterpillar products found fame with the <a href="/wiki/Seabees" class="mw-redirect" title="Seabees">Seabees</a>, Construction Battalions of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>, who built <a href="/wiki/Aerodrome" title="Aerodrome">airfields</a> and other facilities in the <a href="/wiki/Asiatic-Pacific_Theater" title="Asiatic-Pacific Theater">Pacific Theater of Operations</a>. Caterpillar ranked 44th among United States corporations in the value of wartime military production contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> During the post-war construction boom, the company grew at a rapid pace and launched its first venture outside the U.S. in 1950, marking the beginning of Caterpillar's development into a <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Expansion_in_developing_markets">Expansion in developing markets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Expansion in developing markets" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9ll_K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n_t%C3%A9r_-_2015.04.10_(1).JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Sz%C3%A9ll_K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n_t%C3%A9r_-_2015.04.10_%281%29.JPG/220px-Sz%C3%A9ll_K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n_t%C3%A9r_-_2015.04.10_%281%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Sz%C3%A9ll_K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n_t%C3%A9r_-_2015.04.10_%281%29.JPG/220px-Sz%C3%A9ll_K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n_t%C3%A9r_-_2015.04.10_%281%29.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sz%C3%A9ll_K%C3%A1lm%C3%A1n_t%C3%A9r_-_2015.04.10_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>CAT 323DL</div></div></div>
<p>Caterpillar built its first Russian facility in the town of <a href="/wiki/Tosno" title="Tosno">Tosno</a>, located near <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg, Russia">St. Petersburg, Russia</a>. It was completed in 16 months, occupied in November 1999, and began fabricating machine components in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> It had the first electrical substation built in the <a href="/wiki/Leningrad_Oblast" title="Leningrad Oblast">Leningrad Oblast</a> since the Communist government was dissolved on December 26, 1991. The facility was built under harsh winter conditions, where the temperature was below −13 °F (−25 °C). The facility construction was managed by the <a href="/wiki/Lemmink%C3%A4inen_Group" title="Lemminkäinen Group">Lemminkäinen Group</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki,_Finland" class="mw-redirect" title="Helsinki, Finland">Helsinki, Finland</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>The $125M Caterpillar Suzhou, <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a> facility, manufactures medium wheel loaders and motorgraders, primarily for the Asian market. The first machine was scheduled for production in March 2009. URS Ausino, in San Francisco, California, manages facility construction.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Caterpillar has manufactured in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> since 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 2010 the company announced plans to further expand production of <a href="/wiki/Backhoe" title="Backhoe">backhoe</a> and small wheel loaders with a new factory.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>Caterpillar has been manufacturing machines, engines and generator sets in India as well. Caterpillar has 3 facilities in India, which are in the states of Tamil Nadu (Thiruvallur &amp; Hosur) and Maharastra (Aurangabad).    
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Acquisitions" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_lines">Business lines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Business lines" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>Through fiscal year 2010, Caterpillar divided its products, services and technologies into three principal lines of business: machinery, engines and financial products for sale to private and governmental entities.<sup id="cite_ref-about_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-3">[3]</a></sup> Starting in 2011, Caterpillar reports its financials using five business segments: construction industries, resource industries, power systems, financial products, and all other segments.<sup id="cite_ref-Caterpillar-Inc-May-2011-10-Q_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caterpillar-Inc-May-2011-10-Q-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Machinery">Machinery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Machinery" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hydraulicke_demolicni_nuzky_na_podvozku_CAT_330.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Hydraulicke_demolicni_nuzky_na_podvozku_CAT_330.jpg/220px-Hydraulicke_demolicni_nuzky_na_podvozku_CAT_330.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="2304"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Hydraulicke_demolicni_nuzky_na_podvozku_CAT_330.jpg/220px-Hydraulicke_demolicni_nuzky_na_podvozku_CAT_330.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hydraulicke_demolicni_nuzky_na_podvozku_CAT_330.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cat 365B <a href="/wiki/Demolition" title="Demolition">demolition</a> machine in action</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Caterpillar_Inc._machines" title="List of Caterpillar Inc. machines">List of Caterpillar Inc. machines</a></div>
<p>Caterpillar has a list of some 400 products for purchase through its dealer network. Caterpillar's line of machines range from tracked tractors to <a href="/wiki/Excavator" title="Excavator">hydraulic excavators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Backhoe" title="Backhoe">backhoe loaders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grader" title="Grader">motor graders</a>, off-highway trucks, <a href="/wiki/Loader_(equipment)" title="Loader (equipment)">wheel loaders</a>, agricultural <a href="/wiki/Tractor" title="Tractor">tractors</a> and locomotives. Caterpillar machinery is used in the construction, <a href="/wiki/Road_construction" class="mw-redirect" title="Road construction">road-building</a>, mining, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, energy, transportation and material-handling industries.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caterpillar_D350D.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Caterpillar_D350D.jpg/220px-Caterpillar_D350D.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1066" data-file-height="598"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 123px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Caterpillar_D350D.jpg/220px-Caterpillar_D350D.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="123" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caterpillar_D350D.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caterpillar D350D articulated off-road truck</div></div></div>
<p>Caterpillar is the world's largest manufacturer of wheel loaders. The small size wheel loaders (SWL) are designed and manufactured at facilities in <a href="/wiki/Clayton,_North_Carolina" title="Clayton, North Carolina">Clayton, North Carolina</a>. The medium size (MWL) and large size (LWL) are designed at their <a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Illinois" title="Aurora, Illinois">Aurora, Illinois</a> facility. Medium wheel loaders are manufactured at: <a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Illinois" title="Aurora, Illinois">Aurora, Illinois</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sagamihara,_Kanagawa" class="mw-redirect" title="Sagamihara, Kanagawa">Sagamihara, Kanagawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>; <a href="/wiki/Gosselies" title="Gosselies">Gosselies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charleroi" title="Charleroi">Charleroi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>; <a href="/wiki/Piracicaba" title="Piracicaba">Piracicaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="São Paulo, Brazil">São Paulo, Brazil</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>. Large wheel loaders are manufactured exclusively in the United States on three separate assembly lines at Aurora, Illinois.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="On-road_trucks">On-road trucks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: On-road trucks" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar began selling a line of on-road <a href="/wiki/Truck" title="Truck">trucks</a> in 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Cat_CT660" title="Cat CT660">Cat CT660</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Class_8_truck" class="mw-redirect" title="Class 8 truck">Class 8 vocational truck</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>
As of March 2016, Caterpillar has ceased production of on-highway vocational trucks stating that “Remaining a viable competitor in this market would require significant additional investment to develop and launch a complete portfolio of trucks, and upon an updated review, we determined there was not a sufficient market opportunity to justify the investment,” said Ramin Younessi, vice president with responsibility for Caterpillar's Industrial Power Systems Division. “We have not yet started truck production in Victoria, and this decision allows us to exit this business before the transition occurs.”<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Engines_and_gas_turbines">Engines and gas turbines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Engines and gas turbines" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lifeboat_Engines.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Lifeboat_Engines.JPG/220px-Lifeboat_Engines.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Lifeboat_Engines.JPG/220px-Lifeboat_Engines.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lifeboat_Engines.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Twin Caterpillar 3208T engines powering <a href="/wiki/Clogher_Head" class="mw-redirect" title="Clogher Head">Clogher Head</a> lifeboat (Ireland)</div></div></div>
<p>A portion of Caterpillar's business is in the manufacturing of diesel and natural gas engines and <a href="/wiki/Gas_turbines" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas turbines">gas turbines</a> which, in addition to their use in the company's own vehicles, are used as the <a href="/wiki/Prime_mover_(locomotive)" title="Prime mover (locomotive)">prime movers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Diesel_locomotive" title="Diesel locomotive">locomotives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semi-trailer_truck" title="Semi-trailer truck">semi trucks</a>, marine vessels and ships, as well as providing the power source for <a href="/wiki/Peak-load_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Peak-load power plant">peak-load power plants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrical_generator" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical generator">emergency generators</a>.
</p><p>Caterpillar 3116 engine was used up until 1997, when Caterpillar introduced the inline 6 cylinder 7.2 litre <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_3126" title="Caterpillar 3126">Caterpillar 3126</a> engine as its first electronic diesel engine for light trucks and buses.<sup id="cite_ref-EngineBuilder_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EngineBuilder-102">[102]</a></sup> Caterpillar decreased emissions and noise the next year in the 3126B version of the engine, and improved emissions further in 2002 with the 3126E which had an improved high-pressure oil pump and improved electronics.<sup id="cite_ref-EngineBuilder_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EngineBuilder-102">[102]</a></sup> In 2003 Caterpillar started selling a new version of this engine called the <a href="/w/index.php?title=C-7_(diesel_engine)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="C-7 (diesel engine) (page does not exist)">C-7</a> to meet increased <a href="/wiki/United_States_emission_standards" class="mw-redirect" title="United States emission standards">United States emission standards</a> that came into effect in 2004; it had the same overall design as the 3126 version, but with improved fuel injectors and electronics which included its new Advanced Combustion Emissions Reduction Technology (ACERT) system.<sup id="cite_ref-EngineBuilder_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EngineBuilder-102">[102]</a></sup> In 2007, as <a href="/wiki/Ultra-low-sulfur_diesel" title="Ultra-low-sulfur diesel">ultra-low-sulfur diesel</a> became required in North America, Caterpillar updated the C7 to use <a href="/wiki/Common_rail" title="Common rail">common rail</a> fuel injectors and improved ACERT electronics.<sup id="cite_ref-EngineBuilder_102-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EngineBuilder-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2008, Caterpillar announced it would be exiting the on-highway diesel engine market in the United States before updated 2010 <a href="/wiki/U.S._Environmental_Protection_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Environmental Protection Agency">U.S. Environmental Protection Agency</a> (EPA) <a href="/wiki/Emission_standard" class="mw-redirect" title="Emission standard">emission standards</a> took effect,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> as costly changes to the engines, which only constituted a small percentage of Caterpillar's total engine sales, would be likely.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2010, Caterpillar announced it would buy German engine-manufacturer <a href="/wiki/MWM_GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="MWM GmbH">MWM GmbH</a> from <a href="/wiki/3i" title="3i">3i</a> for $810 million.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters.com_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters.com-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Caterpillar_Defense_Products">Caterpillar Defense Products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Caterpillar Defense Products" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Caterpillar Defence Products<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> subsidiary, headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury" title="Shrewsbury">Shrewsbury</a>, United Kingdom, provides diesel engines, automatic transmissions and other parts for the UK's <a href="/wiki/Challenger_2_tank#Titan" class="mw-redirect" title="Challenger 2 tank">Titan</a> <a href="/wiki/Armored_bridge_layer" class="mw-redirect" title="Armored bridge layer">armored bridge layer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Challenger_2_tank#Trojan" class="mw-redirect" title="Challenger 2 tank">Trojan</a> <a href="/wiki/Combat_engineering_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Combat engineering vehicle">combat engineering tank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrier_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrier vehicle">Terrier</a> <a href="/wiki/Combat_engineering_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Combat engineering vehicle">combat engineering vehicles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tank_transporter" title="Tank transporter">tank transporters</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romanian</a> <a href="/wiki/MLI-84" title="MLI-84">MLI-84</a> <a href="/wiki/Armored_personnel_carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Armored personnel carrier">armored personnel carrier</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Swiss</a> <a href="/wiki/Mowag_Piranha" title="Mowag Piranha">Piranha III</a> <a href="/wiki/Light_armored_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Light armored vehicle">light armored vehicle</a>, which is currently being developed for use by American light armored formations; large fleets of military trucks in both the U.S. and UK; and the <a href="/wiki/Combat_Vehicle_90" title="Combat Vehicle 90">CV90</a> family of <a href="/wiki/Infantry_fighting_vehicle" title="Infantry fighting vehicle">infantry fighting vehicles</a> used by the armies of Sweden, Norway, Finland, Switzerland, the Netherlands and Denmark.
</p><p>This division also provides both propulsion engines and power generation systems to the naval <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipbuilding industry">shipbuilding industry</a>, such as the Series 3512B turbocharged V-12 diesel engine for American <a href="/wiki/USS_Virginia_(SSN-774)" title="USS Virginia (SSN-774)"><i>Virginia</i></a> class <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">nuclear submarines</a>. Caterpillar diesel engines are also used in <a href="/wiki/USS_San_Antonio_(LPD-17)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS San Antonio (LPD-17)"><i>San Antonio</i></a> class <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_transport_dock" title="Amphibious transport dock">amphibious transport docks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Spanish</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_de_Baz%C3%A1n_class_frigate" class="mw-redirect" title="Álvaro de Bazán class frigate"><i>Alvaro de Bazán</i> class frigates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">British</a> <a href="/wiki/River_class_patrol_vessel" class="mw-redirect" title="River class patrol vessel"><i>River</i> class</a> <a href="/wiki/Patrol_boat" title="Patrol boat">patrol vessels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Navy" title="Mexican Navy">Mexican</a> <a href="/wiki/Sierra_class_submarine" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra class submarine"><i>Sierra</i> class</a> patrol boats,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Malaysian_Navy" title="Royal Malaysian Navy">Malaysian</a> <a href="/wiki/Kedah_class_OPV" class="mw-redirect" title="Kedah class OPV"><i>Kedah</i> class</a> <a href="/wiki/MEKO" title="MEKO">MEKO</a> A-100 offshore patrol vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The poor network security of the Caterpillar engines puts America's submarine force at risk for <a href="/wiki/Cyberattack" title="Cyberattack">cyberattack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In a recent interview on cybersecurity, the Navy clarified that Caterpillar actually has some of the most secure control systems and will be used as a model of how the Navy will design cyber protections into its control systems.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IDF-D9-Zachi-Evenor-001.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/IDF-D9-Zachi-Evenor-001.jpg/220px-IDF-D9-Zachi-Evenor-001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3513" data-file-height="2912"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 182px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/IDF-D9-Zachi-Evenor-001.jpg/220px-IDF-D9-Zachi-Evenor-001.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="182" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IDF-D9-Zachi-Evenor-001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/IDF_Caterpillar_D9" title="IDF Caterpillar D9">IDF Caterpillar D9</a> armored bulldozer</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> buys bulldozers for the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> (IDF) from Caterpillar through the U.S. government foreign aid money in their civilian configuration. The military modifications and the installment of <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_armor" class="mw-redirect" title="Vehicle armor">vehicle armor</a> are done entirely in Israel by the IDF and Israeli security contractors (<a href="/wiki/Israel_Military_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="Israel Military Industries">Israel Military Industries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Israel_Aerospace_Industries" title="Israel Aerospace Industries">Israel Aerospace Industries</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The IDF uses many Caterpillar machines such as <a href="/wiki/Bulldozer" title="Bulldozer">bulldozers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Excavator" title="Excavator">excavators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheel_loader" class="mw-redirect" title="Wheel loader">wheel loaders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grader" title="Grader">graders</a> mainly for engineering, <a href="/wiki/Earthworks_(engineering)" title="Earthworks (engineering)">earthworks</a> and building projects. The most famous machine in use by the IDF's <a href="/wiki/Combat_Engineering_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Combat Engineering Corps">Combat Engineering Corps</a> is the heavy <a href="/wiki/IDF_Caterpillar_D9" title="IDF Caterpillar D9">IDF Caterpillar D9</a> <a href="/wiki/Armored_bulldozer" title="Armored bulldozer">armored bulldozer</a>, which is being used also for <a href="/wiki/Combat_engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Combat engineering">combat engineering</a> and combat missions under fire.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a>' use of highly modified <a href="/wiki/Caterpillar_D9" title="Caterpillar D9">Caterpillar D9</a> bulldozers has led to Caterpillar being criticized by activists and some shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> In particular, the <a href="/wiki/IDF_Caterpillar_D9" title="IDF Caterpillar D9">IDF Caterpillar D9</a> was involved in an incident in 2003, in which the American activist <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Corrie" title="Rachel Corrie">Rachel Corrie</a> was killed by a bulldozer. A lawsuit against Caterpillar by her family and families of Palestinians, who were also killed by Caterpillar equipment, was unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-sun_corrie_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sun_corrie-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reuters_appeals_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters_appeals-114">[114]</a></sup> A lawsuit against <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Israeli_Defense_Ministry" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli Defense Ministry">Israeli Defense Ministry</a> was rejected by the court, ruling that her death was an accident, caused by restricted field of view from the heavily armored operators' cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> In 2014 <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">Presbyterian Church (USA)</a> sold its shares in Caterpillar citing the use of Caterpillar bulldozers involved in <a href="/wiki/House_demolition_in_the_Israeli-Palestinian_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="House demolition in the Israeli-Palestinian conflict">demolition and surveillance activities in the West Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cooperman2004-09-29_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cooperman2004-09-29-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TimesOfIsrael_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimesOfIsrael-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Caterpillar_Electronics">Caterpillar Electronics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Caterpillar Electronics" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Caterpillar Electronics business unit has formed Caterpillar Trimble Control Technologies LLC (CTCT), a 50:50 joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Trimble_Inc" class="mw-redirect" title="Trimble Inc">Trimble Inc</a>. CTCT develops positioning and control products for earthmoving and paving machines in the construction and mining industries, using technologies such as GNSS, optical total stations, lasers and sonics. The products are used in a range of applications where the operator of the machine benefits from having accurate horizontal and vertical guidance. CTCT is based in <a href="/wiki/Dayton,_Ohio" title="Dayton, Ohio">Dayton, Ohio</a>, and started its operations on April 1, 2002.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_products">Agriculture products</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Agriculture products" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar introduced the <i>Challenger</i> range of agricultural <a href="/wiki/Tractors" class="mw-redirect" title="Tractors">tractors</a> as the result of several development programs over a long period of time. The program started in the 1970s and involved both D6-based units and Grader power units. A parallel program was also developing wheeled high hp tractors based on using the articulated loading shovel chassis was latter merged with the crawler team. The result was the Challenger Tractor and the "Mobi-Trac" system.
</p><p>The Challenger has been marketed in Europe as <a href="/wiki/Claas" title="Claas">Claas</a> machines since 1997, with Caterpillar marketing the Claas-built Lexion combine range in the USA. Claas and Caterpillar formed a joint venture, <i>Claas Omaha</i>, to build <a href="/wiki/Combine_harvester" title="Combine harvester">combine harvesters</a> in Omaha, Nebraska, USA under the <i>CAT</i> brand. In 2002, Cat sold its stake to Claas, and licensed the use of <i>CAT</i> and the CAT yellow livery to Claas. They are marketed as <i>Lexion</i> combines now.
</p><p>Also in 2002, Caterpillar sold the <i>Challenger</i> tracked tractor business to <a href="/wiki/AGCO" title="AGCO">AGCO</a> and licensed the use of the Challenger and CAT names and livery to them. This ended Cat's venture into agriculture.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_products_and_brand_licensing">Financial products and brand licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Financial products and brand licensing" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar provides financing and insurance to customers via its worldwide dealer network <sup id="cite_ref-about_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-3">[3]</a></sup> and generates income through the licensing of the Caterpillar and CAT trademarks and logos.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Brand_licensing">Brand licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Brand licensing" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caterpillar-brand_work_boot.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Caterpillar-brand_work_boot.jpg/220px-Caterpillar-brand_work_boot.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Caterpillar-brand_work_boot.jpg/220px-Caterpillar-brand_work_boot.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caterpillar-brand_work_boot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Caterpillar-branded work boots manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Wolverine_World_Wide" title="Wolverine World Wide">Wolverine World Wide</a></div></div></div>
<p>Caterpillar sells the right to manufacture, market and sell products bearing the Cat trademark to licensees worldwide. <a href="/wiki/Wolverine_World_Wide" title="Wolverine World Wide">Wolverine World Wide</a> is one example, a licensee since 1994 and currently the sole company licensed to produce Cat branded <a href="/wiki/Footwear" title="Footwear">footwear</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-wolverine_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wolverine-118">[118]</a></sup> Other licensees sell items including scale models of Cat products, clothing, hats, luggage, watches, flashlights, shovels, knives, fans, gloves, smartphones<sup id="cite_ref-Liszewski_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liszewski-119">[119]</a></sup> and other consumer products.<sup id="cite_ref-cat_watches_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cat_watches-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-suresource_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-suresource-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Manufacturing" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar products and components are manufactured in 110 facilities worldwide. 51 plants are located in the United States and 59 overseas plants are located in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> (until 2015), <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, Canada, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>), <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.
</p><p>Caterpillar's historical manufacturing home is in Peoria, Illinois, which also has been the location of Caterpillar's world headquarters and core research and development activities. Although Caterpillar has contracted much of its local parts production and warehousing to third parties, Caterpillar still has four major plants in the Peoria area: the <a href="/wiki/Mapleton,_Illinois" title="Mapleton, Illinois">Mapleton</a> Foundry, where diesel engine blocks and other large parts are cast; the <a href="/wiki/East_Peoria,_Illinois" title="East Peoria, Illinois">East Peoria</a> factory, which has assembled Caterpillar tractors for over 70 years; the <a href="/wiki/Mossville,_Illinois" title="Mossville, Illinois">Mossville</a> engine plant, built after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Morton,_Illinois" title="Morton, Illinois">Morton</a> parts facility.
</p><p>Major facilities in Europe:
</p>
<ul><li>Belgium: <a href="/wiki/Gosselies" title="Gosselies">Gosselies</a> (1965): Hydraulic Excavators, Medium Wheel Loaders, components (factory closed in 2016)</li>
<li>France: <a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89chirolles" title="Échirolles">Échirolles</a> (1961): Track Type Tractors, Track Type Loaders, Wheeled Excavators, Undercarriage components</li>
<li>Hungary: <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6d%C3%B6ll%C5%91" title="Gödöllő">Gödöllő</a>: Fabrications, Buckets</li>
<li>Italy: <a href="/wiki/Minerbio" title="Minerbio">Minerbio</a>: Paving Products</li>
<li>Poland: <a href="/wiki/Sosnowiec" title="Sosnowiec">Sosnowiec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jan%C3%B3w_Lubelski" title="Janów Lubelski">Janów Lubelski</a>: Fabrications</li>
<li>Russia: <a href="/wiki/Tosno" title="Tosno">Tosno</a>: Fabrications</li>
<li>UK: <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>: Mini-excavators; <a href="/wiki/Peterlee" title="Peterlee">Peterlee</a>: Articulated Dump Trucks; <a href="/wiki/Peterborough" title="Peterborough">Peterborough</a>: Engines; <a href="/wiki/Larne" title="Larne">Larne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>: generating sets.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></li></ul><p>Major facilities in Latin America:
</p>
<ul><li>Mexico: <a href="/wiki/Torre%C3%B3n" title="Torreón">Torreón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acu%C3%B1a_Municipality" title="Acuña Municipality">Acuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monterrey" title="Monterrey">Monterrey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reynosa_Municipality" title="Reynosa Municipality">Reynosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Potos%C3%AD" title="San Luis Potosí">San Luis Potosí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tijuana" title="Tijuana">Tijuana</a></li>
<li>Brazil: <a href="/wiki/Campo_Largo,_Paran%C3%A1" title="Campo Largo, Paraná">Campo Largo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Piracicaba" title="Piracicaba">Piracicaba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">Curitiba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hortol%C3%A2ndia" title="Hortolândia">Hortolandia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sete_Lagoas" title="Sete Lagoas">Sete Lagoas</a> </li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Remanufacturing">Remanufacturing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Remanufacturing" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Major facilities in Latin America:
</p>
<ul><li>Mexico: <a href="/wiki/Oradel_Industrial_Center" title="Oradel Industrial Center">Oradel Industrial Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuevo_Laredo" title="Nuevo Laredo">Nuevo Laredo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamaulipas" title="Tamaulipas">Tamaulipas</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9xico" class="mw-redirect" title="México">México</a> (Since 1988)<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Distribution">Distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Distribution" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar products are distributed to end-users in nearly 200 countries through Caterpillar's worldwide network of 220 dealers. Caterpillar's dealers are independently owned and operated businesses with exclusive geographical territories. Dealers provide sales, maintenance and repair services, rental equipment, and parts distribution. <a href="/wiki/Finning_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Finning International">Finning</a>, a dealer based in Vancouver, Canada, is Caterpillar's largest global distributor.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gmmco_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Gmmco Ltd">Gmmco Ltd</a> is India's No. 1 Dealer for Caterpillar Machines.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p><p>Most dealers use a management system called DBS for their day-to-day operations.
</p><p>As of the first quarter of 2006, 66% of Caterpillars sales are made by one of the 63 dealers in the United States, with the remaining 34% sold by one of Caterpillar's 157 overseas dealers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Management" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar has a <a href="/wiki/Corporate_governance" title="Corporate governance">corporate governance</a> structure where the <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_board" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman of the board">chairman of the board</a> also acts as chief executive officer (CEO). The board of directors is fully independent and is made up of non-employee <a href="/wiki/Non-executive_director" title="Non-executive director">directors</a> selected from outside the company. Several <a href="/wiki/President_(corporate_title)" title="President (corporate title)">group presidents</a> report to the CEO, and multiple vice presidents report to each group president.
</p><p>The board has three committees: audit; compensation and human resources; governance and public policy.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p><p>The behavior of all employees is governed by a code of worldwide business conduct, first published in 1974 and last amended in 2005, which sets the corporate standard for honesty and ethical behavior. Management employees are retested on this code annually.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_board_of_directors">Current board of directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Current board of directors" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
