<p>On January 1, 2017, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Umpleby" title="Jim Umpleby">Jim Umpleby</a> succeeded <a href="/wiki/Douglas_R._Oberhelman" title="Douglas R. Oberhelman">Douglas R. Oberhelman</a> as CEO and Dave Calhoun became non-executive chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> On December 12, 2018, Umpleby was named chairman of the board as well, reversing Caterpillar's previous decision to split the CEO and chairman position.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Workforce_and_labor_relations">Workforce and labor relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Workforce and labor relations" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>As of December 31, 2009, Caterpillar employed 93,813 persons of whom 50,562 are located outside the United States. Current employment figures represent a decline of 17,900 employees compared the third quarter of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_2009_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K_2009-4">[4]</a></sup> Due to the restructuring of business operations which began in the 1990s, there are 20,000 fewer <a href="/wiki/Labor_union" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor union">union</a> jobs in the Peoria, Illinois area while employment outside the U.S. has increased.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Labor_practices">Labor practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Labor practices" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar came close to bankruptcy in the early 1980s, at one point losing almost US$1 million per day due to a sharp downturn in product demand as competition with Japanese rival <a href="/wiki/Komatsu_Limited" title="Komatsu Limited">Komatsu</a> increased. (At the time, Komatsu used the internal slogan "encircle Caterpillar".)<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Caterpillar suffered further when the United States declared an <a href="/wiki/United_States_embargoes" class="mw-redirect" title="United States embargoes">embargo</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> after the Soviet invasion of <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, causing the company to be unable to sell US$400 million worth of pipelaying machinery that had already been built.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p><p>Due to the drastic drop in demand, Caterpillar initiated employee <a href="/wiki/Layoffs" class="mw-redirect" title="Layoffs">layoffs</a>, which led to strikes, primarily by the members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers">United Auto Workers</a>, against Caterpillar facilities in <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>. Several news reports at the time indicated that products were piling up so high in facilities that replacement workers could barely make their way to their work stations.
</p><p>In 1992, the <a href="/wiki/United_Auto_Workers" title="United Auto Workers">United Auto Workers</a> conducted a five-month strike against Caterpillar. In response, Caterpillar threatened to replace Caterpillar's entire unionized work force. Over ten thousand UAW members struck again in 1994–1995 for 17 months, a record at that time. The strike ended with the UAW deciding to return to work without a contract despite record revenues and profits by Caterpillar.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In 1994, Caterpillar offered a contract to the UAW members that would have raised the salary of top workers from $35,000 to $39,000 per year. However, the UAW was seeking the same top wage of $40,000 that was paid to workers at Deere &amp; Company in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p><p>During the strikes, Caterpillar used management employees in an attempt to maintain production. It suspended <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> work, sending thousands of engineers and other non-bargained for employees into their manufacturing and assembly facilities to replace striking or locked out union members.
</p><p>Rather than continuing to fight the United Auto Workers, Caterpillar chose to make itself less vulnerable to the traditional bargaining tactics of organized labor. One way was by outsourcing much of their parts production and warehouse work to outside firms. In another move, according to UAW officials and industry analysts, Caterpillar began to execute a "southern strategy".<sup id="cite_ref-southernstrategy_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-southernstrategy-135">[135]</a></sup> This involved opening new, smaller plants, termed "focus facilities", in <a href="/wiki/Right-to-work_law" title="Right-to-work law">right-to-work</a> states. Caterpillar opened these new facilities in <a href="/wiki/Clayton,_North_Carolina" title="Clayton, North Carolina">Clayton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanford,_North_Carolina" title="Sanford, North Carolina">Sanford, North Carolina</a>; <a href="/wiki/Greenville,_South_Carolina" title="Greenville, South Carolina">Greenville, South Carolina</a>; <a href="/wiki/Corinth,_Mississippi" title="Corinth, Mississippi">Corinth, Mississippi</a>; <a href="/wiki/Dyersburg,_Tennessee" title="Dyersburg, Tennessee">Dyersburg, Tennessee</a>; <a href="/wiki/Griffin,_Georgia" title="Griffin, Georgia">Griffin</a> and <a href="/wiki/LaGrange,_Georgia" title="LaGrange, Georgia">LaGrange, Georgia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Seguin,_Texas" title="Seguin, Texas">Seguin, Texas</a>; and <a href="/wiki/North_Little_Rock,_Arkansas" title="North Little Rock, Arkansas">North Little Rock, Arkansas</a>.
</p><p>In 2012, the company locked out workers at a locomotive plant in London, Ontario, Canada and demanded some accept up to a 50% cut in pay, in order to become cost-competitive with comparable Caterpillar manufacturing facilities in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The move created controversy in Canada, with some complaining the plant was acquired under false pretenses.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Retail store <a href="/wiki/Mark%27s_Work_Wearhouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark's Work Wearhouse">Mark's Work Wearhouse</a> began pulling Caterpillar boots from its shelves as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p><p>On May 1, 2012, 780 members of the International Association of Machinists and Aerospace Workers Local Lodge 851 went on strike. An agreement was reached in August, resulting in a 6-year wage freeze. Striking workers expressed anger about the freeze given the company's record 2011 profits and CEO Oberhelman's 60% salary increase.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Environmental record" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_stewardship">Environmental stewardship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Environmental stewardship" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar divisions have won Illinois Governor's Pollution Prevention Awards every year since 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Caterpillar was awarded the 2007 Illinois Governor's Pollution Prevention Award for three projects: The Hydraulics and Hydraulic Systems business unit in Joliet implemented a flame sprayed coating for its truck suspension system, replacing a chroming process, reducing hazardous waste by 700,000 pounds annually and saving 14 million US gallons (53,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of water. Caterpillar's Cast Metals Organization in Mapleton worked with the American Foundry Society to help produce a rule to reduce hazardous waste in scrap metal that meet strict quality requirements, and also allow foundries to continue recycling certain types of scrap and maintain a competitive cost structure. Caterpillar's Mossville Engine Center formed a team to look at used oil reuse and recycle processes that forced MEC to send large amounts of used oil off-site for recycling, and developed an updated system for reclaiming it for reuse on-site. The resulting benefits included a usage reduction of about 208,000 US gallons (790 m<sup>3</sup>) of oil per year.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p><p>Caterpillar in 2004 participated in initiatives such as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a>'s National Clean Diesel Campaign program, which encourages retrofitting fleets of older buses and trucks with newer diesel engines that meet higher emissions standards.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, Caterpillar donated $12 million to <a href="/wiki/The_Nature_Conservancy" title="The Nature Conservancy">The Nature Conservancy</a> in a joint effort to protect and preserve river systems in Brazil, U.S.A., and China.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p><p>Caterpillar has, for many years, been a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Business_Council_for_Sustainable_Development" title="World Business Council for Sustainable Development">World Business Council for Sustainable Development</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Geneva,_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva, Switzerland">Geneva, Switzerland</a><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> and has been listed on the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Sustainability_World_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Dow Jones Sustainability World Index">Dow Jones Sustainability World Index</a> each year since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Clean_Air_Act_violation">Clean Air Act violation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Clean Air Act violation" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In July 1999, Caterpillar and five other <a href="/wiki/Diesel_engine" title="Diesel engine">diesel engine</a> manufacturers signed a <a href="/wiki/Consent_decree" title="Consent decree">consent decree</a> with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Justice Department</a> and the <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">State of California</a>, after governmental investigations revealed violations of the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a>. The violation involves over a million diesel engines sold with <a href="/wiki/Defeat_device" title="Defeat device">defeat devices</a>, devices that regulated emissions during pre-sale tests, but that could be disabled in favor of better performance during subsequent highway driving. Consequently, these engines "...emit up to triple the permissible level of smog-forming <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a> (NOx). In 1998 alone, these violating vehicles emitted 1.3 million tons of additional NOx – an amount equal to the emissions of 65 million cars." For this reason, Caterpillar was named the "Clean Air Villain of the Month" for August 2000 by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Clean_Air_Trust&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Clean Air Trust (page does not exist)">Clean Air Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> The consent decree provided that $83 million be paid in civil penalties and determined new deadlines for meeting emissions standards. Caterpillar, however, was successful in lobbying for an extension of deadlines they considered too severe. Even so, in October 2002, Caterpillar – the only diesel engine company (of those that signed decrees) to fail to meet the new emissions standards deadline – was forced to pay $128 million in per-engine non-conformance penalties.<sup id="cite_ref-doj2003_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doj2003-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_deferral_techniques">Tax deferral techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Tax deferral techniques" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In March 2017, when US federal agents raided Caterpillar's headquarters in Peoria Ill., it was already evident that the company engaged in aggressive measures to control tax costs. Since April 2014, the company's tax policies have been investigated by a senate subcommittee headed by Senator <a href="/wiki/Carl_Levin" title="Carl Levin">Carl Levin</a>. Those investigations uncovered significant changes in Caterpillar's offshore tax strategy, culminating in the creation of the new Swiss subsidiary Caterpillar SARL (CSARL) in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>. In 1999, the former Caterpillar executive Daniel Schlicksup accused the company of funneling profits from replacement parts to Switzerland where it had no warehouses or factories. The Internal Revenue Service found the firm liable for a billion dollars of unpaid taxes for the years 2007 to 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Fine_Mess_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Fine_Mess-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>At the same time, the architect of Caterpillar's fiscal strategy, <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> (PWC) came also under scrutiny, owing this to a conflict of interest, acting as Caterpillar's global tax consultant and controller.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> The Senate uncovered documents from PWC saying the elaborate move was simply a way to evade American taxes. "We are going to have to do some dancing" one said. Another noted, "What the heck, we will all be retired when this comes up on audit."<sup id="cite_ref-A_Fine_Mess_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_Fine_Mess-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel_Defense_Forces_sales">Israel Defense Forces sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Israel Defense Forces sales" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2004 the Office of the <a href="/wiki/UN_High_Commissioner_on_Human_Rights" class="mw-redirect" title="UN High Commissioner on Human Rights">UN High Commissioner on Human Rights</a> sent a warning letter to the company about its sales of bulldozers to the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> (IDF) and which were used in part to destroy Palestinian farms.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Trademark_claims">Trademark claims</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Trademark claims" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Caterpillar Inc. has sought the revocations of <a href="/wiki/Registered_trademark" class="mw-redirect" title="Registered trademark">registered trademarks</a> in the United States incorporating the word "Cat" within the market of apparel, such as "Cat &amp; Cloud" (a cafe in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_California" title="Santa Cruz, California">Santa Cruz, California</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_Cat" title="Keyboard Cat">Keyboard Cat</a>. The company has faced criticism for this perceived "bullying", even when the likelihood of confusion is low.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span id="Advocacy.2C_philanthropy_and_awards"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Advocacy,_philanthropy_and_awards">Advocacy, philanthropy and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Advocacy, philanthropy and awards" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>Caterpillar is a leading member of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Global_Leadership_Coalition" title="U.S. Global Leadership Coalition">U.S. Global Leadership Coalition</a>, a Washington D.C.-based coalition of over 400 major companies and NGOs that advocates for increased funding of American diplomatic and development efforts abroad through the International Affairs Budget.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Economic development projects in developing countries (particularly in rural, agricultural regions) serve as new markets for Caterpillar products by improving political and economic stability and raising average incomes.
2011 recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Henry_C._Turner_Prize_for_Innovation_in_Construction_Technology" title="Henry C. Turner Prize for Innovation in Construction Technology">Henry C. Turner Prize for Innovation in Construction Technology</a> from the <a href="/wiki/National_Building_Museum" title="National Building Museum">National Building Museum</a>.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">September 21,</span> 2014</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=U.S.+Global+Leadership+Coalition&amp;rft.atitle=U.S.+Global+Leadership+Coalition%2C+Global+Trust+members&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.usglc.org%2Fabout%2Four-coalition&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACaterpillar+Inc." class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
</li>
</ol></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Further reading" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<ul><li>Orlemann, Eric C. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=pTvLXD25AbQC&amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;dq=Caterpillar+Chronicle+The+History+of+the+World%27s+Greatest+Earthmovers&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=r-7zSPcctc&amp;sig=VX_BYmaifPrBtON-3HTQGRs5f80&amp;hl=en&amp;ei=W770S8m4LZTcsgO8yb2IBQ&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=1&amp;ved=0CBkQ6AEwAA#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false"><i>Caterpillar Chronicle, The History of the World's Greatest Earthmovers</i></a>. Minneapolis, MN: MBI Publishing Company, 2000. <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7603-3673-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7603-3673-1">978-0-7603-3673-1</a></li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Caterpillar_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: External links" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
